<<fadeinsound "Burial Loop v2.mp3">>\n\nThe chief breaker starts with the limbs, cutting off small sections.\n\nHis cleaver makes a thumping sound with each cut.\n\nHe hands the severed flesh and bone to his assistants.\n\nThey mash it into a pulp with their hammers,\nand mix in the tsampa.\n\n[[next|FendingOffTheVultures]]
My brother and I watch, but we also have a job to do.\n\nBecause the vultures have noticed us.\n\nWe see them, circling down from the cliffs.\n\nMy brother hands me a stick, to fend them off.\nIt is not their time. Yet.\n\n[[next|VultureTime]]\n

They pound down the remaining bones with their hammers,\nand mix in more tsampa.\n\nThis is for the crows and the hawks.\n\nOur Grandfather is generous. He will feed everyone.\n\n[[next|Afternoon]]
I grow tired and return to our room.\n\nTomorrow will be a long day.\n\nMy brother remains, listening to the chanting,\nwatching over Grandfather’s body.\n\n[[next|Night]]
The vultures descend on Grandfather’s body.\n\nThe peck and tear with their beaks. \nThey swallow great chunks of flesh.\n\nThey eat. And eat.\n\n[[next|Mashing]]\n
<<fadeoutsound "Menu Loop.mp3">>\n<<fadeinsound "Night Loop.mp3">>\n\nI am waiting for a yak.\n\nAgain.\n\n[[next|ItHasBeenYears]]
<<fadeoutsound "Burial Loop v2.mp3">>\n\n<<fadeinsound "Outside Loop.mp3">>\n\n\nWe look at the monastery down below.\n\nTomorrow I will return to the city.\n\nMy brother will return to our village.\n\nOn his way back he will set the yak free.\nThe yak is expensive, but this is the proper way.\n\nWe will not meet again for many years.\nUntil one of us is generous to the birds.\n\n[[next|FinalTitle]]
The yak carries something on its back.\n\nA long white bundle.\n\nA body.\n\nOur grandfather.\n\n[[next|MainTitle]]
<<fadeoutsound "Night Loop.mp3">>\n\n[img[body_breakers]]\n\nBODY BREAKERS\n\n<<playsound "Body Breakers - Title.mp3">>\n\n[[next|InTheMonastery]]
My brother tells me about grandfather.\n\n“After Grandmother died he stayed active,\ntending the sheep and yaks.”\n\nBut he was never the same.\n\n[[next|HeBecameSick]]
They body breakers look like the other monks, except for what they carry.\n\nOne carries a hatchet and a cleaver. He is the chief.\n\nHis assistant carry hammers and pouches of tsampa,\nthe mixture of barley flour and yak butter.\n\n[[next|TheyLaugh]]
By the afternoon, there is nothing left.\n\nThe body breakers go back down the hill.\n\nMy brother and I remain.\n\n[[next|Ending]]
